  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer12994232824789026490">With undertones of vampires, Frankenstein, dragons' hoards, and killing fields, Matt's story turns out to be an inspiring tale of friendship, survival, hope, and transcendence. A must-read for teenage fantasy fans.<br/><br/>At his coming-of-age party, Matteo Alacrán asks El Patrón's bodyguard, "How old am I?...I know I don't have a birthday like humans, but I was born." <br/><br/>"You were ha</span>
  <span id="freeText12994232824789026490" style="display:none">With undertones of vampires, Frankenstein, dragons' hoards, and killing fields, Matt's story turns out to be an inspiring tale of friendship, survival, hope, and transcendence. A must-read for teenage fantasy fans.<br /><br />At his coming-of-age party, Matteo Alacrán asks El Patrón's bodyguard, "How old am I?...I know I don't have a birthday like humans, but I was born." <br /><br />"You were harvested," Tam Lin reminds him. "You were grown in that poor cow for nine months and then you were cut out of her." <br /><br />To most people around him, Matt is not a boy, but a beast. A room full of chicken litter with roaches for friends and old chicken bones for toys is considered good enough for him. But for El Patrón, lord of a country called Opium—a strip of poppy fields lying between the U.S. and what was once called Mexico—Matt is a guarantee of eternal life. El Patrón loves Matt as he loves himself for Matt is himself. They share identical DNA.</span>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/96684300-rogue-dragon"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/96684300-rogue-dragon">Rogue Dragon</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent"> As a 13-year-old, having read it at the age of 12, I believe that 13 is a good age to read The House of the Scorpion. There are several instances in <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent"> As a 13-year-old, having read it at the age of 12, I believe that 13 is a good age to read The House of the Scorpion. There are several instances in which dark and possibly scary themes emerge, so this book should only be read by confident readers in their early teens. This book contains instances of violence, abuse, and ethical issues concerning cloning, as well as drug use and religious debate. However, this should not tarnish the excellence of this book, as it deserves the Newbery Medal, and is a well-written book full of good messages and ideas.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/678887-how-do-you-think-experiences-effect-you">How do you think experiences effect you? In the book, two people are exactly alike, but they aren&#39;t exactly alike at the same time, they both view things differently and act differently but they both have the same DNA..... So, why is that?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_678887'><a id="like_count_community_question_678887" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/678887?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F13376.The_House_of_the_Scorpion">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/678887-how-do-you-think-experiences-effect-you">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/678887-how-do-you-think-experiences-effect-you">See all 5 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/121008062-tully"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/121008062-tully">Tully</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Nurture (environment) and Nature (DNA-genes). We are shaped different by our environment. Identical twins who live separately end up having similar fe<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Nurture (environment) and Nature (DNA-genes). We are shaped different by our environment. Identical twins who live separately end up having similar features but different personalities. Similar, because they can also have different heights and build depending on their resources. I've read some journal studies about it. It's expected, because we form our belief systems and behavior based on the people around us and the media we are exposed to. Ultimately, the way we respond to stimuli would be different.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_228992318" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228992318" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228992318?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780439579292" href="/book/show/13377.The_House_of_the_Scorpion">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=dystopia-utopia">dystopia-utopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228992318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8799501275553284798"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>This book has been on my goodreads shelf since pretty much the beginning of time... so why on earth have I been wasting my time with every other poorly-constructed dystopian world instead of reading this? I have absolutely no excuse: I own a copy, it's won practically every award going, and all my reviewer friends have been constantly singing its praises. Perhaps I am way more influenced by title and cover than I like to admit - though there's nothing actually <i>wrong</i> with either, I still feel</span>
  <span id="freeText8799501275553284798" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>This book has been on my goodreads shelf since pretty much the beginning of time... so why on earth have I been wasting my time with every other poorly-constructed dystopian world instead of reading this? I have absolutely no excuse: I own a copy, it's won practically every award going, and all my reviewer friends have been constantly singing its praises. Perhaps I am way more influenced by title and cover than I like to admit - though there's nothing actually <i>wrong</i> with either, I still feel like this doesn't scream at me "awesome dystopian setting + interesting questions about what it means to be human!!". It's good. Really good. If you liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/764347.Unwind__Unwind___1_" title="Unwind (Unwind, #1) by Neal Shusterman" rel="nofollow noopener">Unwind</a>, then you should also like this.<br><br>I loved the setting - Mexico - and it was obvious to me that the author was very familiar with Mexican culture and legends, she incorporates a lot of this into the story. I suppose one of the quickest ways to mess up your novel is to write about places and things you don't have a clue about, but I still really wish more authors would try to use different settings. There's a whole world out there that I'm not in a position to explore right now so I like to pretend I'm there by visiting other countries in books. Plus, is it that hard to do a little research on a country's culture, traditions and legends (etc.)?<br><br>In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13376.The_House_of_the_Scorpion__Matteo_Alacran___1_" title="The House of the Scorpion (Matteo Alacran, #1) by Nancy Farmer" rel="nofollow noopener">The House of the Scorpion</a> we are immediately introduced to a boy called Matt who is a clone that was grown in a cow and harvested. The man who shares his DNA is El Patron, the extremely rich head of a huge opium empire and a man with the power to deliver to himself a longer than usual life with the help of clones. Matt's relationship with El Patron is conflicted. On one hand, Matt knows he is evil and corrupt - he plants chips in people's heads to make them obey his orders without question - but Matt also knows that El Patron is himself. They are both intelligent and talented individuals, Matt acknowledges multiple times how alike the two people are. But Matt is treated by others as an animal, they do not see how anything grown in a cow can be human and some of the treatment he endured really pissed me off, never mind the fact that his genetic make-up is identical to El Patron's.<br><br>Matt questions himself and the world around him throughout the book. He finds it hard to believe that El Patron could possibly mean him harm - because how could you harm yourself? It's also a look at what makes someone human and how easy it is for people to dehumanize and convince themselves that a person is nothing more than an animal. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13376.The_House_of_the_Scorpion__Matteo_Alacran___1_" title="The House of the Scorpion (Matteo Alacran, #1) by Nancy Farmer" rel="nofollow noopener">The House of the Scorpion</a>, in my opinion, could only be improved by removing that chunk of story after <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Matt escapes <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It felt at odds with the rest of the book and it was clearly the author's attempt to quickly drop in one more big issue - socialism - but it just felt forced and wasn't needed, it's not like we don't already have enough to go on with all the ethical questions flying around in this novel. Take that out and this book would be five stars. But anyway, it's still a really great story about cloning and about humanity that will probably make you want to punch several of the characters at times. But, as with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/534258.Sisters_in_Sanity" title="Sisters in Sanity by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">Sisters in Sanity</a>, I seem to like books that make me furious, guess they just make me care more.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8799501275553284798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_6069227" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6069227" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/325341-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6069227?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/325341-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780689852220" href="/book/show/866611.The_House_of_the_Scorpion">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6069227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16408757511909507425">This is one of the almost perfect books written for young adults. It is an exciting story that will keep you turning the pages, but it also makes you think about the world we live in. It is a Newbery and Printz honor book and winner of the National Book Award.<br/><br/>In the House of the Scorpion, Nancy Farmer tells the story of Matt, the clone of 142-year-old El Patron, dictator of Opium, a country between the United States and Aztlan. In Opium, clones have one purpose, to extend the lives of those whos</span>
  <span id="freeText16408757511909507425" style="display:none">This is one of the almost perfect books written for young adults. It is an exciting story that will keep you turning the pages, but it also makes you think about the world we live in. It is a Newbery and Printz honor book and winner of the National Book Award.<br /><br />In the House of the Scorpion, Nancy Farmer tells the story of Matt, the clone of 142-year-old El Patron, dictator of Opium, a country between the United States and Aztlan. In Opium, clones have one purpose, to extend the lives of those whose DNA they possess by providing them with a source for spare parts. The brains of most other clones are destroyed at birth, but Matt’s is left intact on the orders of El Patron. At the beginning of the novel, Matt knows none of these things. He is cared for in isolation by El Patron’s cook, Celia, who loves him. He only becomes aware that he is different from other people when he becomes a resident at El Patron’s estate where he is viewed not as a human, but as an unclean animal without a soul. Matt is educated and lives in luxury, but is looked on with disgust by most of the estate’s inhabitants. The exceptions are Celia, El Patron’s bodyguard Tam Lin, and Maria, one of the children who discovered him. These three people see the humanity in him and teach him to be a good person.<br /><br />Farmer does a masterful job of creating the world that Matt lives in from the cloning technology to the old fashioned ways on the estate which is designed to replicate the Mexico of El Patron’s youth over 100 years ago. El Patron has made his fortune capturing Mexicans attempting to cross the border into the United States and using them to grow opium. To ensure that they don’t escape, implants in their brains make them completely devoid of free will to the extent that they will not eat or drink without being told to do so. The threat of being turned in to one of these “eejits” is sufficient to allow El Patron to control others. The reader’s interest is sustained by discovering along with Matt and from his point of view, the workings Opium, his purpose in life, and his ultimate fate. With the help of Celia and Tam Lin, he escapes to Aztlan where he is no longer treated as subhuman, but is captured and forced to labor with other orphans under the control of guards called “keepers” who relentlessly practice behavioral control methods to keep the young workers at the plankton factory in line. This is a coming of age story with a difference.<br /><br />House of the Scorpion is a chilling story because Farmer portrays a world that just may be possible. Cloning is already a reality. There are people in today’s world just as invisible to the larger society as the orphans. Child slavery exists. Environmental degradation is occurring. Matt’s escape from his future as a clone gives that reader hope that good will prevail in this world as well.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16408757511909507425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_34386309" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34386309" />
    <a title="Jack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/102625-jack"><img alt="Jack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1233330430p2/102625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34386309?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack" href="/user/show/102625-jack">Jack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/102625-jack?shelf=teen">teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34386309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17933557407740505773">A really hit and miss book, with some terrific ideas and terrible plotting.<br/><br/>The main character, Matt, is a clone of the world's biggest drug kingpin, the 140+ year-old El Patron. Matt lives in El Patron's sprawling estate and is hated by most of the residents there, aside from his care-taker Celia and El Patron himself, who is raising Matt for his own sinister reasons. Soon, these reasons are revealed and Matt's only hope is to escape.<br/><br/>This felt like it should have been at least twice as long. The</span>
  <span id="freeText17933557407740505773" style="display:none">A really hit and miss book, with some terrific ideas and terrible plotting.<br /><br />The main character, Matt, is a clone of the world's biggest drug kingpin, the 140+ year-old El Patron. Matt lives in El Patron's sprawling estate and is hated by most of the residents there, aside from his care-taker Celia and El Patron himself, who is raising Matt for his own sinister reasons. Soon, these reasons are revealed and Matt's only hope is to escape.<br /><br />This felt like it should have been at least twice as long. The author, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8360.Nancy_Farmer" title="Nancy Farmer" rel="nofollow noopener"> Nancy Farmer</a> has developed an intriguing world, extrapolating from the US and Mexico's current problems with drugs, illegal immigration, and pollution, and also addresses ethical and legal issues around cloning. However, as compelling as this world is, it never feels real or adequately developed, and she has a ridiculous habit of explaining important aspects of how the world she has created operates at just the time they become pertinent to the plot. The characters are a mixed bag as well: they're likable and believable except when they're not, and turn from fully-realized creations to cardboard cut-outs whenever they have to do something that advances the story.<br /><br />This isn't to say that I didn't like the book, necessarily. It was a great coming of age story, and I think that young teenagers will really enjoy the characters and the action. This book also won a whole mess of awards, which admittedly may color my reaction to it. I just wish that more time had been spent developing the characters, the world, and the mess of ideas that were introduced.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17933557407740505773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1349614676" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1349614676" />
    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1349614676?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1349614676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8857344634309532308"><i>The House of the Scorpion</i> is really unlike any YA/middle grade book I've ever read. It's extremely philosophical and thought-provoking, covering topics of the soul, identity, and human rights in a very intriguing way.<br/><br/>It takes place in some distant future where there is a land between the U.S. and Mexico that grows poppies for opium. The main character Matt is a clone of the leader of the nation named El Patron. El Patron seems kind and generous, giving his clone an education and privileges that </span>
  <span id="freeText8857344634309532308" style="display:none"><i>The House of the Scorpion</i> is really unlike any YA/middle grade book I've ever read. It's extremely philosophical and thought-provoking, covering topics of the soul, identity, and human rights in a very intriguing way.<br /><br />It takes place in some distant future where there is a land between the U.S. and Mexico that grows poppies for opium. The main character Matt is a clone of the leader of the nation named El Patron. El Patron seems kind and generous, giving his clone an education and privileges that other clones are not usually afforded. But as Matt gets older he begins to learn more about his life and his country's history that conflicts with what he has been told.<br /><br />It's a tale of coming-of-age set against a survival/dystopian storyline with really complex material. I would be wary of giving this book to young readers, as it can be a bit graphic at times and deals with some sensitive issues. But I can imagine reading this book in middle school and having really great discussions surrounding it.<br /><br />Apparently there is a sequel that I was told you don't have to read to get the whole story, but I'm very curious to see what happens next. So I plan on picking that one up eventually.<br /><br />For fans of <i>The Chaos Walking Trilogy</i> and other dystopian/sci-fi/survival stories, this is a really great read, and I would recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8857344634309532308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_73404410" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/73404410" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/73404410?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781439106556" href="/book/show/8235474-the-house-of-the-scorpion">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=national-book-award">national-book-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=newbery">newbery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=printz">printz</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73404410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3000393745556309415">As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/05/ya-review-the-house-of-the-scorpion-by-nancy-farmer.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/><a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/category/she%20made%20me%20do%20it/1.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Flannery made me do it</a> and I am pleased that she did. I have no idea why I've been avoiding <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13376.The_House_of_the_Scorpion' title='The House of the Scorpion by Nancy Farmer' rel='nofollow noopener'>The House of the Scorpion</a> for so long. Just look at its accolades - National Book Award Winner, Printz Honoree, Newbery Honoree. It practically has my name written on it.<br/><br/>But, is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13376.The_House_of_the_Scorpion' title='The House of the Scorpion by Nancy Farmer' rel='nofollow noopener'>The House of the Scorpion</a> worth such an overwhelming acclaim though?<br/><br/>I'd say, its first 215 pages and the last 20 are (ebook edition).<br/><br/>The first two thirds of the book are riveting. This story is not just </span>
  <span id="freeText3000393745556309415" style="display:none">As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/05/ya-review-the-house-of-the-scorpion-by-nancy-farmer.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br /><br /><a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/category/she%20made%20me%20do%20it/1.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Flannery made me do it</a> and I am pleased that she did. I have no idea why I've been avoiding <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13376.The_House_of_the_Scorpion" title="The House of the Scorpion by Nancy Farmer" rel="nofollow noopener">The House of the Scorpion</a> for so long. Just look at its accolades - National Book Award Winner, Printz Honoree, Newbery Honoree. It practically has my name written on it.<br /><br />But, is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13376.The_House_of_the_Scorpion" title="The House of the Scorpion by Nancy Farmer" rel="nofollow noopener">The House of the Scorpion</a> worth such an overwhelming acclaim though?<br /><br />I'd say, its first 215 pages and the last 20 are (ebook edition).<br /><br />The first two thirds of the book are riveting. This story is not just a clone story. (For some reason, the majority of stories about clones focus on exactly the same things.) Yes, it is horrifying in how it examines the (familiar) debate about a clone's humanity and soulless(ful)ness. Matt is a clone and is defined by people around him as livestock, a source of body parts, and not a human being. (How can he be human if he was grown in and harvested from a cow?) Nancy Farmer takes Matt's character on a journey of self-discovery and self-awareness that allows him to accept that he is not what he is told he is, that he is as much of a human being as any person around him. It is a compelling journey, even though its sentiment isn't particularly new to me - I've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6334.Never_Let_Me_Go" title="Never Let Me Go by Kazuo Ishiguro" rel="nofollow noopener">Never Let Me Go</a> and watched <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0399201/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Island</a>.<br /><br />But, thankfully, there is more to distinguish <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13376.The_House_of_the_Scorpion" title="The House of the Scorpion by Nancy Farmer" rel="nofollow noopener">The House of the Scorpion</a> from similar stories.<br /><br />First, the novel is set in Mexico (well, a future version of it). This country's life is written richly and authentically and never feels like just an exotic backdrop. I am no expert on Mexican culture though, so I might have felt that in awe of it as portrayed in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13376.The_House_of_the_Scorpion" title="The House of the Scorpion by Nancy Farmer" rel="nofollow noopener">The House of the Scorpion</a> because of the narrator of the audio, who infused Mexican flavor into the story most organically.<br /><br />Second, this is a story of a drug lord and his enslaved family. El Patrón feels he is owed a few generations worth of life, and he will stop at nothing to get what he thinks he is entitled to. Cloning is a part of his plan for immortality. It's in Matt's relationship with his master and owner where the story shines the most. How would a clone feel about the person who is identical to him, the source of his life? Would he be able to hate him, essentially hating himself? If a clone's genetic make-up is similar to that of a ruthless criminal, does it mean that this clone is destined to follow the same path and become the same vicious person? Or is there a way to break away from the prototype? And how would a master feel about his own clone? Would it be possible for him to treat this younger version of himself as an organ bank, or there exists a connection that is closer than even that between a father and a child? These questions had my brain working, and this part of the book was 5-star material for me.<br /><br />But then came the escape part, in the last third of the book, and I found myself struggling with it. I was bored, I didn't feel like those pages (3-months of Matt's life worth) connected well thematically with the overreaching story arc, I didn't think they were necessary, I didn't think that a whole set of new characters (including villains) needed to be introduced so late in the story, and I surely didn't think that anti-socialist rants needed to come into play. (How did they relate to Matt's journey?) I thought, those pages only occupied time with no real bearing on the rest of the novel. To me, those 80 pages could have been completely cut out.<br /><br />Thankfully, the ending did save <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13376.The_House_of_the_Scorpion" title="The House of the Scorpion by Nancy Farmer" rel="nofollow noopener">The House of the Scorpion</a>. It happens so infrequently in books, but it did bring the story full circle to El Patrón, and it was satisfying. But that big chunk of the novel, unfortunately, made me much less willing to recommend it, even though during the first part of the book I kept thinking this novel would be a great fit for fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/764347.Unwind__Unwind___1_" title="Unwind (Unwind, #1) by Neal Shusterman" rel="nofollow noopener">Unwind</a>. I might reread <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13376.The_House_of_the_Scorpion" title="The House of the Scorpion by Nancy Farmer" rel="nofollow noopener">The House of the Scorpion</a> in future, but I'll be sure to skip over a big part of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3000393745556309415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_610838231" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/610838231" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/610838231?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=21th-century">21th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=science">science</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer610838231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15417263357967202757">The House of the Scorpion (Matteo Alacran #1), Nancy Farmer<br/><br/>The story is set in the country of Opium, a narrow strip of land between Mexico, and the United States, which is ruled by Matteo Alacran, or El Patron, an incredibly powerful drug lord who is over 140 years old. Opium consists of several drug-producing Farms, of which the Alacran estate (which produces opium poppies) is the largest. The protagonist, Matt, is a clone of El Patron. For the first six years of his life, he lives in a small h</span>
  <span id="freeText15417263357967202757" style="display:none">The House of the Scorpion (Matteo Alacran #1), Nancy Farmer<br /><br />The story is set in the country of Opium, a narrow strip of land between Mexico, and the United States, which is ruled by Matteo Alacran, or El Patron, an incredibly powerful drug lord who is over 140 years old. Opium consists of several drug-producing Farms, of which the Alacran estate (which produces opium poppies) is the largest. The protagonist, Matt, is a clone of El Patron. For the first six years of his life, he lives in a small house on the edge of the poppy fields with Celia, a cook working in El Patron's mansion. When he is discovered by three children, Emilia and Steven and Maria, he smashes a window and jumps out of the house. Unaware of the danger of jumping barefoot onto smashed glass, he has to be carried to El Patron's mansion and treated for his injuries. Matt is treated kindly until Mr. Alacrán, El Patron's great-grandson, recognizes him as a clone, resulting in a few months where he is locked in a room and treated like an animal. When he finds out, El Patron is furious, but gives Matt clothes and his own room and commands everyone to treat him with respect. Matt is also given a bodyguard, Tam Lin, a reformed terrorist, who becomes a father figure to him. He lives in the house for the next seven years and befriends Maria, a friendship that gradually blossoms into romance. Matt is kept in the dark about his identity, however, until a cruel joke reveals to him that he is a clone. Matt also discovers that all clones are supposed to be injected when "harvested" (born) with a compound that cripples their brains and turns them into little more than thrashing, drooling animals meant to donate organs. In denial, he convinces himself that El Patron would not hire tutors for him and keep him entertained if he were intending to kill him, and that instead he must be wanted to run the country when El Patron dies.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز هشتم ماه ژانویه سال 2005 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: خ‍ان‍ه‌ ع‍ق‍رب‌؛ نویسنده: ن‍ان‍س‍ی‌ ف‍ارم‍ر‏‫؛ م‍ت‍رج‍م‌ وی‍دا اس‍لام‍ی‍ه‌؛ تهران، نشر علم، 1383؛ در 543 ص؛ شابک: 9644053931؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 21 م<br /><br />شخصیت اصلی این داستان علمی تخیلی پسر بچه‌ ای ست، به نام «میتو آلاکران»، که به طور غیر طبیعی متولد شده است. او در اصل، از سلول زنده‌ ی انسان دیگری ست، که پس از کشت دادن در بدن یک گاو، به وجود آورده‌ اند. اکثر اطرافیان «مت - متیو آلاکران» او را نه یک پسر بچه، بلکه یک جانور می‌دانند. در اتاقی پر از خاک اره‌ در یک مرغدانی، زندگی می‌کند، جز سوسک‌ها دوستی ندارد، و بهترین اسباب‌ بازی‌هایش، استخوان‌های مانده‌ ی مرغها هستند. اما از نظر «ال پاترون»، فرمانروای کشوری به نام «تریاکستان»، باریکه‌ ای از مزارع خشخاش، که در ناحیه‌ ای میان ایالات متحده‌ ی آمریکا و کشوری واقع شده، که روزگاری «مکزیک» نام داشته است، «مت» در حکم ضمانتی برای زندگی ابدی اوست. «ال پاترون» همانقدر که خودش را دوست میدارد، «مت» را نیز دوست دارد، چرا که «مت» خود ایشانست. «دی.ان.آی.» آن‌ها کاملا یکسان است. «مت» برای درک هستی خویش، با تهدید‌های گروهی از شخصیت‌های شوم، روبرو می‌شود، که خانواده‌ ی تشنه به قدرت «ال پاترون» نیز، در میان این گروه هستند. دور تا دور او را، سپاهی از محافظین خطرناک، و همچنین برده‌ های بی‌عقلی گرفته‌ اند، که ابلهانی مرده مغز هستند، و در مزارع خشخاش «تریاکستان» کشت و زرع می‌کنند. حتی فرار از قلمرو «آلاکران» نیز، برای «مت»، آزادی را به ارمغان نمی‌آورد. زیرا رفتار و شخصیت متفاوتش، او را در میان دیگران انگشت‌ نما می‌کند. ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="15417263357967202757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_101085140" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101085140" />
    <a title="Wicked Incognito Now" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/541201-wicked-incognito-now"><img alt="Wicked Incognito Now" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337228064p2/541201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101085140?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wicked Incognito Now" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wicked Incognito Now" href="/user/show/541201-wicked-incognito-now">Wicked Incognito Now</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101085140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10028425000799820243">I HATED IT, and hated it on so many levels I truly do not know where to begin.<br/><br/>First of all, I will acknowledge one aspect of the story that I found positive. This is the story of Matt, a clone. Matt is raised in a shack on the opium plantation of drug lord, El Patron. He is El Patron's clone, grown for the purpose of being spare body parts for El Patron. In this world (the near future), clones are considered property, livestock. The embroyos are implanted in cows, so the people of this world hav</span>
  <span id="freeText10028425000799820243" style="display:none">I HATED IT, and hated it on so many levels I truly do not know where to begin.<br /><br />First of all, I will acknowledge one aspect of the story that I found positive. This is the story of Matt, a clone. Matt is raised in a shack on the opium plantation of drug lord, El Patron. He is El Patron's clone, grown for the purpose of being spare body parts for El Patron. In this world (the near future), clones are considered property, livestock. The embroyos are implanted in cows, so the people of this world have come to the conclusion that anything born from cows is not human. After they are "born," their brains are purposely damaged so that the people can further consider these clones as beasts instead of human abominations of nature. This campaign of dehumanization has resonance throughout history. The Jews, the enslaved Africans in America, any person of possible Arab descent today....all of these races have undergone a campaign of dehumanization. Those in power subtly manipulated the general population until that population was able to excuse widespread cruelty in their own minds. We always look at those historical periods with disgust and wonder how anyone could ever accept that level of cruelty, and yet it happens over and over again throughout history.<br /><br /><br />A few reasons why I did NOT like this novel: <br /><br />1. The author cannot seem to find her main point or theme. If her theme is the importance of individuality, I think she fails. The book ends with something that complete negates a theme that highlights the importance of individuality---so it can't be that.<br /><br />2. The author's knowledge of cloning is all wrong. She attempts to sway her audience against the entire IDEA without fully understanding the concept. Clones would not be exact copies of their DNA donors. Environment is almost as largely responsible for who we are as our DNA is. At one point, I think she is going to explore this knowledge further, but I ended up being convinced that she just doesn't KNOW that even PHYSICAL traits are affected by environmental factors. Fingerprints are even affected by the force and pressure of things happening in the womb. Identical twins have the same DNA, and yet they are not identical. The same basic principles apply to clones. So, the thing that happens at the end...impossible. <br /><br />3. The plot is all over the place. It has no direction.<br /><br />4. The characterizations are flat. The emotions are hollow. The reader has no background for anyone, or sense of setting.<br /><br />5. The author breaks the cardinal rule of writing: "Show! Don't tell!!" She tells and tells and tells, but never SHOWS us anything. For instance, we are TOLD that the character of Steven is "okay." He's apparently the one character in this drug lord's family that is not evil. Yet, we are not SHOWN this. Why is Steven "okay?" How does Matt know this? Then, when Steven betrays Matt, are we supposed to be appalled? We have no emotional attachment to Steven. Why did we think he WOULDN'T betray Matt?<br /><br />6. Like I said, there is no continuity. No over-arching theme. After leaving the compound, Matt goes to another country. Once there it seems that this story is devolving into a diatribe on socialism. Which, irritated me INCREDIBLY. I couldn't be more sick of this "evils of socialism" storyline. However, at least going on about socialism was giving this novel a POINT!!!! YET, it didn't commit to the evil socialism theme. It turned out that the government was something else entirely. So, I don't know what that bit about the socialist orphanage was. It was completely out of place.<br /><br />Then....the story devolved further....and went a place that left me completely flummoxed and angry that I wasted my time with this horrible written dreck (Matt at one point says: I was, quite literally, the underdog. Oh really Ms. Author? Was he LITERALLY an underdog? Not figuratively?).<br /><br />Ultimately, I am most angry that this type of fiction is winning awards. That our children are assigned badly-written propaganda to read in high school English instead of quality literature.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10028425000799820243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Esther" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Esther" href="/user/show/172571-esther">Esther</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Esther by: </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34335462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16758665894214557342">Recommended to me by my teenaged son, the book had a promising start and an interesting middle, but it all kind of fell apart towards the end and finished with a very unsatisfying ending. I liked the ideas presented about prejudice and predetermination vs. self-determination, and about the relative values of evil. The book is chock-full of evil-doers, some of whom are despicable, some of whom are loved, and one, the most interesting character of them all, Tam Lin, who is a compelling mixture of </span>
  <span id="freeText16758665894214557342" style="display:none">Recommended to me by my teenaged son, the book had a promising start and an interesting middle, but it all kind of fell apart towards the end and finished with a very unsatisfying ending. I liked the ideas presented about prejudice and predetermination vs. self-determination, and about the relative values of evil. The book is chock-full of evil-doers, some of whom are despicable, some of whom are loved, and one, the most interesting character of them all, Tam Lin, who is a compelling mixture of sin and repentance, loyalty and betrayal, an evil-doer who also manages to be a good man.<br /><br />It felt like after presenting all her ideas and laying out the moral dilemmas, the author kind of ran out of steam and dashed off an ending that, I suppose, she figured would tie up all the loose ends, but really leaves just about everything hanging.<br /><br />For instance, in a workhouse/orphanage setting that makes the Dickens orphans look positively privileged (at least they get <i>genuine</i> gruel), we are let to believe that all abuses will be corrected once one of the orphans manages to get word out that they are being mistreated. I guess the world would be a much better place than is portrayed in this book (or in reality, for that matter) if that was all it took to overcome evil and corruption.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16758665894214557342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_246821135" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/246821135" />
    <a title="Reynje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje"><img alt="Reynje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473722441p2/5590906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/246821135?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynje" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje">Reynje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8352767-the-house-of-the-scorpion">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246821135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15609919274026264882"><blockquote>
  <i>But underneath Matt felt a hollowness. He understood he was only a photograph of a human, and that meat he wasn’t really important. Photographs could lie forgotten in drawers for years. They could be thrown away.</i>
</blockquote> You know that moment just before you’ve entirely woken up, when you’re dreaming, but you’re conscious that you’re dreaming, so you’re hovering somewhere between sleep and wakefulness? <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Or is that just me? <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> That’s the closest I can get to describing the e</span>
  <span id="freeText15609919274026264882" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>But underneath Matt felt a hollowness. He understood he was only a photograph of a human, and that meat he wasn’t really important. Photographs could lie forgotten in drawers for years. They could be thrown away.</i>
</blockquote> You know that moment just before you’ve entirely woken up, when you’re dreaming, but you’re conscious that you’re dreaming, so you’re hovering somewhere between sleep and wakefulness? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Or is that just me? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> That’s the closest I can get to describing the experience of reading The House of the Scorpion. The world of this book blends the familiar with the strange, the safe with the sinister, in a singularly unsettling and powerful way. <br /><br />It took me some time to reach that conclusion. Throughout large parts of this book, I felt almost disconnected - held at arm’s length by the characters and struggling against the slow pace of the plot. As a reader who generally prefers emotionally immersive books, I found myself at something of a loss as to define how I felt about this one. I still do, to an extent. <br /><br />What was clear, after I finished The House of the Scorpion, was that it was lingering with me. I was still thinking about the characters and the things that had happened to them, but most of all, the extremely disquieting questions this story poses. <br /><br />At the risk of sounding like I just want to get out of writing a synopsis, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[which is also true, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> in my opinion the less known about this story before approaching it the better. Farmer chooses to tell her story in a particular manner, peeling back layer upon layer to reveal the frightening realities of what initially appears to be a quite familiar world. <br /><br />This novel takes on complex subjects. Presents difficult scenarios. Gives you a false sense of security then pulls the floor out from under you. Asks you to question the characters, the world, even yourself. Relentlessly demands that you don’t just <i>read</i> this book, but that you be consumed by it’s central paradox. <br /><br />Matteo <i>is</i> El Patron. But are there infinite possible versions of the exact same person? How much of who we are is written into out genetic code and how much is shaped by external things? How does choice factor into the way we develop, and what if those choices are never presented? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Am I thinking about this too much? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The House of the Scorpion does require you to just roll with it, for want of a better expression, with respect to some elements of the story. But for me, it was this shifting from the firmly realistic to the speculative that gave this book the slightly surreal atmosphere that I came to enjoy. <br /><br />I do think that given the nature of some of the events (and I apologise for being deliberately vague her - actually for the whole vagueness of this review in general), I should have felt closer, more emotionally involved in the story. While I did become entirely engaged in the plot, I can’t say that this was due to a particular sense of connection with the characters. I <i>wanted</i> to feel more invested in them, yet I just… wasn’t. <br /><br />That said, I can’t deny that this is a powerful book. It’s quite unlike anything I’ve read before, and it wasn’t what I was expecting. But it’s a thought provoking, quietly intense story that well-deserves it’s recognition. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15609919274026264882" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780439579292" href="/book/show/13377.The_House_of_the_Scorpion">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39941297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3945741208076452776">Yeah, yeah, yeah. See the RACK of medals of the cover of this book? A friend told me she felt this novel changed the face of science-fiction. High praise indeed. I didn't buy the hype, and still have issues with the extremely slow start of this novel. It has been sitting on my desk for almost two years (no lie) and I finally read it. <br/><br/>After the first 80 pages of slow moving material, I finally became vested in the characters and thought the novel finally caught on. I think this novel probably doe</span>
  <span id="freeText3945741208076452776" style="display:none">Yeah, yeah, yeah. See the RACK of medals of the cover of this book? A friend told me she felt this novel changed the face of science-fiction. High praise indeed. I didn't buy the hype, and still have issues with the extremely slow start of this novel. It has been sitting on my desk for almost two years (no lie) and I finally read it. <br /><br />After the first 80 pages of slow moving material, I finally became vested in the characters and thought the novel finally caught on. I think this novel probably does change the face of Sci-Fi for MG audiences, because the novel tackles some pretty high-brow concepts (modern slavery, cloning, organ harvesting, Communism, Marxism, Drugs and drug trafficking, addiction, adoption, forgiveness) and like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2493.Lois_Lowry" title="Lois Lowry" rel="nofollow noopener">Lois Lowry</a>'s book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3636.The_Giver" title="The Giver by Lois Lowry" rel="nofollow noopener">The Giver</a> Farmer does not shy away from these complexities.<br /><br />I appreciated the way that Farmer finishes the book, unlike Lowry who closes with ambiguity, Farmer lays it all out on the table. Sequel??? I also predicted the ending with about 200 pages left to go in this book, which I guess is okay because I am a Sci-Fi aficionado and not a sixth-grader. The book for me as an adult probably would get a 3.5 stars, but I thought Farmer handled the material for her intended audience very well, hence the five star rating. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3945741208076452776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7212518980421437476"> The house of the Scorpion is a book about a clone named Matteo Alacran. He was cloned from El Patron and harvested from a cow. His mother like figure is a woman named Celia. When Matteo, "Matt" lives with Celia he doesn't understand that he is different from everyone else. When he is brought from his little house in the poppy field to "The Big House," his life changes for the better and worse. He meets a girl he likes, named Maria, who also likes him, but he is treated like dirt from all of the</span>
  <span id="freeText7212518980421437476" style="display:none"> The house of the Scorpion is a book about a clone named Matteo Alacran. He was cloned from El Patron and harvested from a cow. His mother like figure is a woman named Celia. When Matteo, "Matt" lives with Celia he doesn't understand that he is different from everyone else. When he is brought from his little house in the poppy field to "The Big House," his life changes for the better and worse. He meets a girl he likes, named Maria, who also likes him, but he is treated like dirt from all of the other people living in the house. For six months he lives like an animal, until the day Maria's father sends El Patron a letter explaining to him what has been happening to his clone. When El Patron comes to "The Big House", everything is changed, and whenever El Patron is around Matt, he is treated like a regular person, but when he is gone, Matt is back to being treated like dirt. <br /> This is a book that is full of suspense, action, mystery, and even a bit of horror. This book will make you cry and make you laugh, but no matter what you will definitely enjoy this book. I am not a reader, and I love this book even though it is so long. This is probably the best book I have read in a very long time and I suggest this book to everyone. This is a fictional book, but it is written so well that even though you know everything is fake, you still feel so bad for Matt. When your reading this book it's so intense so you feel like you are part of the book, and that is my opinion of The house of the Scorpion.</span>

<div id="review_634345851" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/634345851" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/634345851?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer634345851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1741894777545231934">First things first: I need to mention I received this book in Goodreads giveaways. I also need to mention that the real rating for this book is <b>3.5 stars</b> as it is better than the majority of the books I rated with 3 stars, but it does not quite reach 4-star rating. I never felt more strongly about having 0.5 star rating on Goodreads since I joined it. <br/><br/>The plot: Matteo Alacran (Matt most of the time) is a clone of a very powerful drug lord El Patron who was created to provide replacement organs f</span>
  <span id="freeText1741894777545231934" style="display:none">First things first: I need to mention I received this book in Goodreads giveaways. I also need to mention that the real rating for this book is <b>3.5 stars</b> as it is better than the majority of the books I rated with 3 stars, but it does not quite reach 4-star rating. I never felt more strongly about having 0.5 star rating on Goodreads since I joined it. <br /><br />The plot: Matteo Alacran (Matt most of the time) is a clone of a very powerful drug lord El Patron who was created to provide replacement organs for the latter. The problem was, El Patron also wanted to have somebody who reminded him about his childhood - and who is the better candidate than his own clone? As a result Matt's brain was not destroyed unlike other clones' that were created for other people. So we have an intelligent almost-but-not-quite human being on one hand and people who regard Matt as something lower than an animal on the other hand. It does not help any that El Patron's clan members hate each other - and everybody else for that matter. <br /><br />The book raises a lot of interesting and important questions: cloning, slavery, free will, drug use - just to name a few. The plot itself is interesting if slow in the beginning and way too fast in the end. <br /><br />Now for the bad parts: the characters that surround Matt at El Patron's residence are all two-dimensional without exceptions. Matt himself is a typical Mary Sue, I always thought about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18254.Oliver_Twist" title="Oliver Twist by Charles Dickens" rel="nofollow noopener">Oliver Twist</a> when I read the first part of the book. Once the book switches to other places, we finally get interesting people and interactions between them - other than just blind hate. <br /><br />I already mentioned plot moving way too slow in the beginning and being rushed in the end. I can actually point to the particular place in the text where the author decided it is time to wrap up everything; the result is that the end feels very simplistic and unfinished. <br /><br />All in all this is not a bad book, but I expected it to be much better from the amount of awards it received. It did not help any that I was reading an adult dystopia book at the same time which had more depth. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1741894777545231934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1959584448" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Cindy Newton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6082517-cindy-newton"><img alt="Cindy Newton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432075684p2/6082517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1959584448?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy Newton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy Newton" href="/user/show/6082517-cindy-newton">Cindy Newton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=ya-books-read">ya-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1959584448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6827961824836954719">I read this to preview for future class use, and I'm very enthusiastic about possibly using it as a whole-class read in the future. It's chockfull of great issues to be explored in class discussions and writing assignments. Best of all, it is a compelling story that will definitely engage even our more reluctant readers.<br/><br/>In addition to that, I enjoyed it personally. Farmer creates a dystopian world that is believable due to the fact that it is based on so many of the issues we are dealing with to</span>
  <span id="freeText6827961824836954719" style="display:none">I read this to preview for future class use, and I'm very enthusiastic about possibly using it as a whole-class read in the future. It's chockfull of great issues to be explored in class discussions and writing assignments. Best of all, it is a compelling story that will definitely engage even our more reluctant readers.<br /><br />In addition to that, I enjoyed it personally. Farmer creates a dystopian world that is believable due to the fact that it is based on so many of the issues we are dealing with today: illegal drugs, powerful drug cartels, illegal immigration, and cloning. It also addresses more universal themes such as the desire for acceptance, the effects of loneliness and isolation, the limits of love and loyalty, etc. Our kids would not find it hard, I believe, to make the connections between the themes in this book and those of the classic literature we read. We would also be able to explore these topics in more depth through non-fiction pieces during our research unit.<br /><br />Aside from the bounty of educational uses, it's just a great story that keeps you turning the pages! I'd like to read the sequel and see what happens next. That really says it all, doesn't it?</span>
  <a data-text-id="6827961824836954719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1433826115" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1433826115" />
    <a title="booklady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/350218-booklady"><img alt="booklady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591723471p2/350218.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1433826115?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booklady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booklady" href="/user/show/350218-booklady">booklady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/15750137-the-house-of-the-scorpion">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=youth">youth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=2004">2004</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1433826115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer798970872634570479">First read this in 2004 when my daughters were in middle school. It’s an excellent young adult novel about a young man, Matt, who discovers he is ‘clone’ in a futuristic society somewhere between America and Mexico. How Matt—cloned to be the spare ‘parts’ for a wealthy elderly man—grows into adolescence and discovers the truth of his identity, learns who his friends and foes are, the rules of the system in which he lives and how to survive is an incredible story. It really helps you look at huma</span>
  <span id="freeText798970872634570479" style="display:none">First read this in 2004 when my daughters were in middle school. It’s an excellent young adult novel about a young man, Matt, who discovers he is ‘clone’ in a futuristic society somewhere between America and Mexico. How Matt—cloned to be the spare ‘parts’ for a wealthy elderly man—grows into adolescence and discovers the truth of his identity, learns who his friends and foes are, the rules of the system in which he lives and how to survive is an incredible story. It really helps you look at human life and ask what it means to be a human being. What exactly constitutes a human person? Someone born of a mother? Who also had a father? What do we mean by ‘existence’? Awareness? Intelligence? Life? The will to live? Do we consider the needs of the state? <br /> <br />Besides Matt there are others this society takes liberty with, deciding what their level of ‘life’ is to be. It’s the kind of book which will have you asking all kinds of questions and considering many things you might not have thought about before.<br /> <br />Highly recommended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="798970872634570479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_66679894" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66679894" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66679894?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Thomas by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/763271-nancy">Nancy</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66679894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12745861548299311565">“The House of the Scorpion” is about Matteo Alacran, who is the clone of another Matteo Alacran. The original Matteo Alacran, also known as El Patron, was a power-hungry drug-dealer that created an evil empire filled with eejits, or people that have no will. Due to Matt being a clone, he is always treated differently – usually for the worse. He is trapped in the Alacran estate, a large mansion filled with people that have a personal distaste for him. Although he does make a few friends, such as </span>
  <span id="freeText12745861548299311565" style="display:none">“The House of the Scorpion” is about Matteo Alacran, who is the clone of another Matteo Alacran. The original Matteo Alacran, also known as El Patron, was a power-hungry drug-dealer that created an evil empire filled with eejits, or people that have no will. Due to Matt being a clone, he is always treated differently – usually for the worse. He is trapped in the Alacran estate, a large mansion filled with people that have a personal distaste for him. Although he does make a few friends, such as Celia, a maid in the Alacran estate that treats Matt like her own son, Tam Lin, one of El Patron’s bodyguards, and Maria, a very emotional girl that has a large mouth and a big heart. And although El Patron is very kind to Matt, he has a wicked plan in store for him, and it has something to do with Patron being over 140 years old…<br /><br />Finally, a novel worthy of five stars! It has been such a long time since I’ve read one, so, it’s kind of exciting. Anyway, on to my personal opinion of the book. I totally loved everything about it. The characters were well-developed, the world was unique and intriguing, and the plot was very well thought-out. The world Farmer created seemed reminiscent of Neal Shusterman’s “Unwind”, which was also a very good novel. Another thing I liked about this book was that although I’m not a huge fan of Sci-fi novels, the prose and dialogue made everything easier for me to digest. I really cared about the characters, I was (pathetically) almost in tears at the end when I learned about a certain character’s fate. So I would highly recommend this book to everyone I know.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12745861548299311565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
